Nov 22 (Reuters) - Northvolt's financial collapse deals a blow to Europe's plan to set up its own battery industry to power electric cars, stirring a debate about whether it needs to do more to attract investment as startups struggle to catch up with Chinese rivals.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eEurope's biggest hope for an electric vehicle battery champion filed for U.S. Chapter 11 bankruptcy protection on Thursday after talks with investors and creditors including Volkswagen and Goldman Sachs for funding failed.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Swedish company, whose motto is \"make oil history\", has received more than $10 billion in equity, debt and public financing since its 2016 start-up. Volkswagen and Goldman Sachs each own about one fifth of its shares.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNorthvolt said on Friday it needed $1.0-$1.2 billion in new funds under the restructuring process, which it hopes will end by the end of March.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn recent months, it has shrunk the business and cut jobs in a bid to shore up its finances. But it has struggled to produce sufficient volumes of high-quality batteries, and lost a 2 billion euro ($2.1 billion) contract from BMW (BMWG.DE), in June.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat has left Europe's ambitions to build its own battery industry looking a distant dream.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn recent years, Northvolt led a wave of European startups investing tens of billions of dollars to serve the continent's automakers as they switch from internal combustion engines to electric vehicles.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut growth in EV demand is moving at a slower pace than many in the industry projected, and China has taken a huge lead in powering EVs, controlling 85% of global battery cell production, International Energy Agency data shows.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eMaking batteries and cells, the units that store and convert chemical energy into electricity, is a delicate process and doing so at scale is a challenge for any battery maker.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNorthvolt has missed some in-house targets and curtailed production at its battery cells plant in northern Sweden, underscoring the difficulties, Reuters reported on Monday.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\"The biggest issue is that batteries are not easy to make and Northvolt haven’t satisfied the supply demands of their customers - that is a management issue,\" said Andy Palmer, founder of consultancy Palmer Automotive said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“The Chinese are technologically 10 years ahead of the West in batteries. That’s a fact,\" he said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAt least eight companies have postponed or abandoned EV battery projects in Europe this year, including China's Svolt and joint venture ACC, led by Stellantis (STLAM.MI), and Mercedes-Benz (MBGn.DE).\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn 2024, Europe's battery pipeline capacity out to 2030 has fallen by 176 gigawatt-hours, according to data firm Benchmark Minerals. That's equivalent to almost all the current installed capacity in Europe, according to Reuters calculations.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eRETHINK\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSome executives say Europe should do more to attract and support home-grown projects so they can compete with Chinese rivals such as CATL (300750.SZ), and BYD (002594.SZ), opens new tab.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\"Europe needs to rethink how it supports a nascent sector before China eats up the entire value chain, which is due to smart planning,\" said James Frith, European head of Volta Energy Technologies, which specialises in battery and energy storage technology.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAmong its $5.8 billion in debts, Northvolt owes the European Investment Bank (EIB) some $313 million.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eEIB vice president Thomas Östros said it had been a constructive partner to Northvolt, but it needed to safeguard the EIB and EU's interests.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\"It remains the case that Europe has a strategic interest in a European battery industry for electric cars and we will follow developments very closely. But it is much to early to say what the outcome will be,\" he said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Swedish government has repeatedly said it does not plan to take a stake in Northvolt.\u003cbr\u003eOn Friday, Northvolt's outgoing CEO and co-founder Peter Carlsson said he was a \"little worried\" Europe is giving up on its dream of competing with China.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHe said Europe would regret it in 20 years time if it retreated.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\"It's not a straight journey and right now, we're all in a bit of a down in that journey where there's more hesitations, there's more questions on the speed of the transition from the carmakers, from policymakers, from the investor community,\" he told reporters in a call.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eReporting by Marie Mannes in Stockholm, Stine Jacobsen in Copenhagen and Alessandro Parodi in Gdansk. assets to Chinese defence and industrial giant, China North Industries Corp, or Norinco in June.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eGecamines, which owns the lease to Chemaf’s mines, whose copper and cobalt are used in electric vehicles and clean energy infrastructure, was asked by Chemaf to approve the sale, but declined.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eGecamines later submitted an unsolicited bid for the Chemaf assets, deepening a standoff that has been complicated by US officials lobbying against China’s grip on the mineral-rich central African Copperbelt.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eChinese companies are major investors in Congo’s mining sector. CMOC Group is now the world’s biggest cobalt miner as it boosts output at Tenke Fungurume Mine it bought from US-based Freeport-McMoRan just four years ago.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eGecamines offered to pay just under $1 million for the mines and processing plant, and wants to conduct an audit of Chemaf’s debts before structuring a payment plan to settle the borrowing, said the sources, who cannot be named because of the sensitivity of the matter.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eChemaf, whose debts have ballooned to $900 million to $1 billion, needs an additional $300 million to expand output and operate profitably, the sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNorinco has offered between $900 million and $1 billion, including settling Chemaf’s debts and outstanding taxes, one of the sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Chinese miner also pledged to advance Chemaf’s plans to raise copper and cobalt output to about 75,000 metric tons and 25,000 tons, respectively, the source added.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eChemaf, which has been operating for the past 20 years, said on its website it has invested more than $610 million developing the second phase of Etoile and Mutoshi mines.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I can confirm we made a better offer than Norinco did, subject to us conducting due diligence of the debt,” Gecamines chairman Robert Lukama told Reuters.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“And more importantly the government declined, and already informed Chemaf by letter that they will not accept the Norinco transaction and we also confirm that we will not give another chance to anyone else other than ourselves,” Lukama added.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNorinco’s move has drawn scrutiny by the US, with State Department officials lobbying Congo to block the deal, three sources told Reuters. The US wants Congo to find an alternative to Norinco, one of the three sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eCash crunch deepens\u003cbr\u003eThe stalled deal has worsened Chemaf’s finances and if it fails completely, the Congolese miner’s key backers, including Trafigura, may either lend more or risk a prolonged period of uncertainty recovering their investments, the sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“The lenders and creditors of Chemaf have faced significant financial hardship for more than 12 months as a result of money owing to them not being paid in accordance with the terms of loans, credit provided and invoices submitted for payment,” one of the sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eChemaf is only processing stockpiles from its Etoile mine as expansion work at Mutoshi mine was halted when financing dried up, the sources said. The company is struggling to pay the salaries of its 3,500 workers, its power bills and security guards manning the sites, the sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eChemaf declined to comment.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eChemaf entered into a 24-month creditors’ protection agreement in August 2023 that lapses next year. While the miner could also seek interim financing, its lenders want to see the Norinco deal concluded as soon as possible, one of the sources added.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTrafigura, one of the main creditors, declined to comment.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUS officials are also rallying Western companies to consider buying the Chemaf assets, the sources said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNorinco, which was sanctioned by the US since 2021, did not immediately respond to emailed queries. stretches from Florida through Arkansas and into Texas, using at least one type of direct lithium extraction (DLE) technology.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eExxon and other oil companies such as Occidental Petroleum and Equinor are increasingly investing in lithium projects, partly due to their belief that extracting the metal from brine involves similar processes as petroleum extraction.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe LG Chem agreement, which would require Arkansas officials to set a state lithium royalty rate to be finalized, is for up to 100,000 metric tons of the ultralight metal over several years.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe move allows Exxon – which plans to self-fund its Arkansas project – to incorporate LG Chem’s lithium quality specifications into its design plans. South Korea-based LG Chem plans to use the lithium at its Tennessee cathode facility, slated to open next year.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“This is about building a relationship with a company that has the same ambitions as building out the North American (battery) supply chain as us,” Patrick Howarth, head of Exxon’s lithium business, told Reuters.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eExxon expects lithium demand to rise despite US President-elect Donald Trump’s campaign vow to end the “EV mandate,” Howarth said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We know that the world’s going to need a lot more lithium than it’s producing today,” he said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFinancial terms of the deal – including the price per metric ton of lithium that LG Chem would pay Exxon – would be negotiated as part of any final contract. others.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOfficials have been debating a lithium royalty since at least 2018, with tension centering on how the metal should be valued given the cost for equipment to filter it
